### 1) Insert a Wronskian-order reformulation of the mixed bad list

**Where to insert**

Insert immediately after

```latex
\end{remark}
```

for

```latex
\begin{remark}[Exact finite obstruction coefficients for the low-order $4$-point branch]
\label{rem:exact-finite-obstruction-coefficients-low-order-four-point}
...
\end{remark}
```

**Insert**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Wronskian-order reformulation of the mixed low-order list]
\label{rem:wronskian-order-reformulation-mixed-list}
On a good $v_5$-patch one has
\[
Y''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_{u_5},
\qquad
S''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_\lambda,
\qquad
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]
Thus, if
\[
r:=\ord_0 J_\lambda=\ord_0 K_v,
\qquad
q:=\ord_0 J_{u_5}=\ord_0 Y'',
\]
then
\[
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=q+2,
\qquad
\ord_0\mathcal Z=q-r.
\]
Hence the dangerous mixed models
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6)
\]
are exactly the Wronskian order-pairs
\[
(\ord_0J_\lambda,\ord_0J_{u_5})=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,4).
\]

If
\[
J_\lambda(x)=x^rA(x),
\qquad
J_{u_5}(x)=x^rB(x),
\qquad
A(0)\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{B(x)}{A(x)}.
\]
For $r=1$, the coefficients $\kappa_{1,1}$ and $\kappa_{1,3}$ are exactly the
$x^1$- and $x^3$-coefficients of the regularized ratio $B/A$; for $r=2$,
$\kappa_{2,2}$ is exactly the $x^2$-coefficient of $B/A$.

Moreover, since
\[
J_c=J_{v_5}=0,
\]
replacing
\[
u_5\longmapsto u_5+a\,c+b\,v_5+\gamma\,\lambda
\]
changes $J_{u_5}$ only by
\[
J_{u_5}\longmapsto J_{u_5}+\gamma J_\lambda.
\]
Thus the nonconstant Taylor coefficients of $\mathcal Z$ are canonical. In
particular, the currently explicit mixed low-order list is already a finite
Wronskian-ratio obstruction list.
\end{remark}
```

### 2) Insert the Route B structural lemmas and the centered quintic nontriviality lemma

**Where to insert**

Insert immediately after

```latex
\end{remark}
```

for

```latex
\begin{remark}[Centered symmetric-placement Taylor package and diagonal-base local exclusion]
\label{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package}
...
\end{remark}
```

and before

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Realization lemma for lifted germs]
```

**Insert**

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Total centered quintic collapse forces source-level degeneration]
\label{lem:total-centered-quintic-collapse}
On the centered symmetric-placement branch one has
\[
u_5=2\bigl(v\,\delta\alpha+\beta\,\delta u\bigr),
\qquad
v_5=2\bigl(\bar\alpha\,\delta u+\bar u\,\delta\alpha\bigr).
\]
If
\[
u_5\equiv 0,
\qquad
v_5\equiv 0,
\]
then
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
\beta(s) & v(s)\\
\bar\alpha(s) & \bar u(s)
\end{pmatrix}
\binom{\delta u(s)}{\delta\alpha(s)}
=0
\]
as an identity of analytic germs. Consequently, either
\[
\Delta_5(s):=\beta(s)\bar u(s)-v(s)\bar\alpha(s)\equiv 0,
\]
or
\[
\delta u(s)\equiv 0,
\qquad
\delta\alpha(s)\equiv 0.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
This is immediate from the displayed formulas for $u_5$ and $v_5$.
If the $2\times 2$ coefficient matrix has nonzero determinant, then the only
solution is $\delta u=\delta\alpha\equiv 0$. If its determinant vanishes
identically, then $\Delta_5\equiv 0$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Centered tagged quintic witness survives specialization]
\label{lem:centered-tagged-quintic-witness-survives-specialization}
On the tagged slice
\[
(K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)}),
\]
the first centered odd coefficient
\[
U_1
\]
of
\[
u_5(s)=U_1s+U_3s^3+U_5s^5+\cdots
\]
has a nonzero $\kappa\,\eta_2\,q^{(5)}$-coefficient. In particular
\[
U_1\neq 0
\]
on that tagged slice, and hence
\[
u_5(s)\not\equiv 0
\]
as a centered germ.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The centered coefficient formula is
\[
U_1=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_1\bigr).
\]
By the tagged-slice analysis already used in the proof of
Lemma~\ref{lem:no-cancellation-quintic-trace}, the $\eta_2$-slice of $X_1$
is off-diagonal, so
\[
\delta u_1=0,
\]
and the $q^{(5)}$-slice of $X_3$ is diagonal, so
\[
\beta_0=0.
\]
Hence
\[
U_1=2v_0\,\delta\alpha_1
\]
on the tagged slice.

Now use the explicit two-direction computation from the proof of
Lemma~\ref{lem:no-cancellation-quintic-trace}. There one writes
\[
G_0=\diag(a^2,b^2),
\qquad
A=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&u\\u&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
D=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0\\0&d
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and expands
\[
X(\varepsilon,\delta)
=
X_0+\varepsilon U+\delta V+\varepsilon\delta W+O(\varepsilon^2,\delta^2).
\]
The proof gives
\[
U_{12}=-\frac{u}{ab(a+b)}\neq 0,
\qquad
V_{22}=-\frac{d}{2b^3}\neq 0.
\]
Here $U_{12}$ is exactly the tagged $\eta_2$-slice of the off-diagonal channel
$v_0$, while $V_{22}$ is exactly the tagged $q^{(5)}$-slice of the diagonal
difference $\gamma-\alpha=2\delta\alpha_1$. Thus the tagged coefficient of
$v_0\,\delta\alpha_1$ is nonzero. Therefore the tagged coefficient of $U_1$
is nonzero as well.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Centered quintic fixed-sector nontriviality]
\label{cor:centered-quintic-fixed-sector-nontriviality}
On the centered diagonal branch,
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
is not identically zero. Equivalently,
\[
(u_5(s),v_5(s))\not\equiv (0,0).
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:centered-tagged-quintic-witness-survives-specialization},
one has $u_5(s)\not\equiv 0$. Since $I$ and $S$ are linearly independent,
the fixed-sector package $A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S$ cannot vanish
identically.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Valuation form of the septic transport constraint]
\label{lem:valuation-form-septic-transport-constraint}
Assume on the centered branch that
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}
\]
is analytic odd. Write
\[
\ord_s u_5=2m+1,
\qquad
\ord_s v_5=2r+1,
\qquad
r\ge m.
\]
Then
\[
\ord_s v_{7,K_1}\ge \ord_s v_5-\ord_s u_5+1=2(r-m)+1.
\]
Equivalently, if
\[
U_1=\cdots=U_{2m-1}=0,\qquad U_{2m+1}\neq 0,
\]
and
\[
V_1=\cdots=V_{2r-1}=0,\qquad V_{2r+1}\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
\widehat V_1=\widehat V_3=\cdots=\widehat V_{2(r-m)-1}=0,
\]
and the first potentially surviving even coefficient of $\Delta_7$ is
\[
D_{2r+2}=\widehat U_1V_{2r+1}-U_{2m+1}\widehat V_{2(r-m)+1}.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Since $\lambda$ is analytic odd and
\[
\Delta_7=\lambda\,v_5,
\]
one has
\[
\ord_s\Delta_7\ge \ord_s v_5+1=2r+2.
\]
Suppose
\[
\ord_s v_{7,K_1}=2d+1<2(r-m)+1.
\]
Then
\[
\ord_s(u_5v_{7,K_1})=(2m+1)+(2d+1)\le 2r,
\]
whereas
\[
\ord_s(u_{7,K_1}v_5)\ge 1+(2r+1)=2r+2
\]
because $u_{7,K_1}$ is odd. Therefore the leading term of
\[
\Delta_7=u_{7,K_1}v_5-u_5v_{7,K_1}
\]
would occur at order at most $2r$, contradicting $\ord_s\Delta_7\ge 2r+2$.
So
\[
\ord_s v_{7,K_1}\ge 2(r-m)+1.
\]

The coefficient statement is the corresponding triangular coefficient form:
vanishing of
\[
D_2,D_4,\dots,D_{2r}
\]
forces
\[
\widehat V_1,\widehat V_3,\dots,\widehat V_{2(r-m)-1}
\]
to vanish successively, and the first potentially surviving coefficient is
\[
D_{2r+2}=\widehat U_1V_{2r+1}-U_{2m+1}\widehat V_{2(r-m)+1}.
\qedhere
\]
\end{proof}
```

### 3) Add the centered quintic-patch dichotomy theorem

**Where to insert**

Insert immediately after

```latex
\end{remark}
```

for

```latex
\begin{remark}[Parallel $u_5$-patch version]
\label{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version}
...
\end{remark}
```

**Insert**

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Centered quintic-patch dichotomy]
\label{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}
Assume the centered diagonal family is a genuine analytic branch in the
underlying $h$-geometry, and that the centered scalar package from
Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package} holds on that
branch. If
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0,
\]
then after shrinking there exist one-sided punctured subarcs on which at least
one of the following holds:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
so the branch enters a good $v_5$-patch;
\item
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad u_5\neq 0,
\]
so the parallel $u_5$-patch of
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version} applies.
\end{enumerate}
In particular, the centered diagonal branch enters some quintic patch on
one-sided punctured arcs.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-fixed-sector-nontriviality},
at least one of $u_5$ or $v_5$ is a nonzero analytic germ on the centered
branch.

If $v_5\not\equiv 0$, then its zeros are isolated. Since
\[
c(s)=C_0+C_2s^2+\cdots,\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
we also have $c\neq 0$ near the basepoint. On any one-sided punctured arc
where $v_5\neq 0$, define
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]
This is a nonconstant analytic germ. If $M\equiv 0$ on such an arc, then
\[
x'=\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2}\equiv 0,
\]
so $x$ would be constant, contradiction. Hence $M$ is not identically zero on
that arc, and by analyticity its zeros are isolated. After shrinking again, one
obtains
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
i.e. a good $v_5$-patch.

If instead $v_5\equiv 0$, then $u_5\not\equiv 0$. Its zeros are isolated, so
after shrinking to a one-sided punctured arc one has
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad u_5\neq 0,
\]
and the $u_5$-patch of Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version} applies.
\end{proof}
```

### 4) Record the automatic \(u_5\)-patch fallback on good \(M\)-intervals

**Where to insert**

Insert immediately after

```latex
\end{proposition}
```

for

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Linear independence of $1,u_5/c,v_5/c$]
\label{prop:linear-independence-one-u5-over-c-v5-over-c}
...
\end{proposition}
```

**Insert**

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Automatic $u_5$-patch nontriviality on good $M$-intervals]
\label{cor:automatic-u5-patch-nontriviality-good-M-intervals}
On every connected interval
\[
J\subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
one has
\[
u_5\not\equiv 0
\qquad\text{on }J.
\]
Hence, after removing the isolated zeros of $u_5$, the parallel $u_5$-patch is
always available on smaller subintervals of $J$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
If $u_5\equiv 0$ on $J$, then
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c}
\]
would be linearly dependent on $J$, contradicting
Proposition~\ref{prop:linear-independence-one-u5-over-c-v5-over-c}.
\end{proof}
```

### 6) Update the “Current geometric bottleneck” remark

**Where to edit**

In

```latex
\begin{remark}[Current geometric bottleneck]
\label{rem:current-geometric-bottleneck}
...
\end{remark}
```

replace the paragraph beginning

```latex
On the $4$-point side, generic nonmixed odd-order $T_v$-zeros can still
carry preexisting close branches
```

through the sentence

```latex
What remains there is to promote that local diagonal-based calculation to a
theorem-level bridge in the good-patch coordinate $x=v_5/c$.
```

with:

```latex
On the $4$-point side, generic nonmixed odd-order $T_v$-zeros can still
carry preexisting close branches, so the nonmixed branch remains genuinely
live. By contrast, the mixed low-order branch is now organized by four sharper
pieces of structure.

First, its explicit dangerous list is finite:
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\},
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),(1,4),(2,5),
\]
or
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6).
\]

Second, in the centered diagonal local regime the centered odd/even Taylor
package gives a punctured-neighborhood exclusion once the induced odd
collision-side coordinate is valid: no $K_v=0$ or $T_v=0$ points occur
arbitrarily close to the diagonal base there.

Third, the centered quintic fixed-sector package is now known not to vanish
identically on the centered diagonal branch. Indeed the tagged quintic witness
survives centered specialization and forces
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S\not\equiv 0.
\]
So the theorem-level mixed target is no longer a coefficient-level statement
such as $V_1\neq 0$; it is a punctured-arc quintic-patch dichotomy: after
shrinking to one-sided punctured arcs, the centered branch should enter either
a good $v_5$-patch or the parallel $u_5$-patch.

Fourth, if the $v_5$-patch fails and $v_5$ starts late, the valuation form of
the septic transport constraint forces matching late vanishing of
$v_{7,K_1}$. Thus failure of the $v_5$-route is not isolated but part of a
coupled quintic--septic degeneration tower.
```

Then replace the next sentence block

```latex
So the missing lifted ingredient is not a blanket zero-capture theorem. It is:
a global branch-continuation / non-recurrence theorem for the nonmixed lifted
$4$-point branches; a theorem-level centered-to-patch parity bridge for the
mixed branch; and, more generally, a global theorem preventing reappearance of
the same line-incidence data on nonadjacent branches.
```

with:

```latex
So the missing lifted ingredient is no longer a vague analysis of the mixed

dichotomy on the mixed side; and, as backup local algebra, exclusion of the
```

## Edit A. Strengthen the centered quintic-patch dichotomy proposition

Right now the proposition still assumes \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0\), even though the draft now proves that unconditionally via the centered tagged witness lemma and the centered quintic fixed-sector nontriviality corollary. So I would remove that assumption and make the proposition itself unconditional.

**Find**
```latex
\begin{proposition}[Centered quintic-patch dichotomy]
\label{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}
Assume the centered diagonal family is a genuine analytic branch in the
underlying $h$-geometry, and that the centered scalar package from
Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package} holds on that
branch. If
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0,
\]
then after shrinking there exist one-sided punctured subarcs on which at least
one of the following holds:
...
\end{proposition}
```

**Replace with**
```latex
\begin{proposition}[Centered quintic-patch dichotomy]
\label{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}
Assume the centered diagonal family is a genuine analytic branch in the
underlying $h$-geometry, and that the centered scalar package from
Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package} holds on that
branch. Then, after shrinking, there exist one-sided punctured subarcs on which
at least one of the following holds:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
so the branch enters a good $v_5$-patch;
\item
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad u_5\neq 0,
\]
so the parallel $u_5$-patch of
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version} applies.
\end{enumerate}
In particular, the centered diagonal branch enters some quintic patch on
one-sided punctured arcs.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-fixed-sector-nontriviality},
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0,
\]
so at least one of $u_5$ or $v_5$ is a nonzero analytic germ on the centered
branch.

If $v_5\not\equiv 0$, then its zeros are isolated. Since
\[
c(s)=C_0+C_2s^2+\cdots,\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
we also have $c\neq 0$ near the basepoint. On any one-sided punctured arc
where $v_5\neq 0$, define
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]
This is a nonconstant analytic germ. If $M\equiv 0$ on such an arc, then
\[
x'=\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2}\equiv 0,
\]
so $x$ would be constant, contradiction. Hence $M$ is not identically zero on
that arc, and by analyticity its zeros are isolated. After shrinking again, one
obtains
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
i.e. a good $v_5$-patch.

If instead $v_5\equiv 0$, then $u_5\not\equiv 0$. Its zeros are isolated, so
after shrinking to a one-sided punctured arc one has
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad u_5\neq 0,
\]
and the $u_5$-patch of Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version} applies.
\end{proof}
```

This reflects the fact that the centered quintic nontriviality lemma is now already proved in the draft. turn97file1

## Edit B. Add the explicit punctured-\(v_5\)-patch promotion corollary

This is a nice theorem-level “goodie” that is now implicit but not stated. It is useful because it isolates the original \(v_5\)-promotion theorem as a corollary of the stronger patch dichotomy.

**Insert immediately after** `\end{proposition}` for `prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy`:

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Conditional punctured $v_5$-patch promotion]
\label{cor:conditional-punctured-v5-patch-promotion}
Under the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}, if
\[
v_5\not\equiv 0
\]
on the centered diagonal branch, then after shrinking there exist one-sided
punctured subarcs contained in
\[
\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}.
\]
Hence on such arcs
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
is automatically a valid local coordinate.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
This is exactly the first branch of the proof of
Proposition~\ref{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}.
\end{proof}
```

This captures one of the main structural findings from the later discussion without changing the architecture.

## Edit C. Replace the “two distinct parity routes” WIP remark

The nonmixed paragraph is fine, but the mixed paragraph should reflect that the theorem-level target is no longer “prove \(V_1\neq 0\)” or even only “transfer centered parity,” but rather “open a quintic patch, then transfer parity on the \(v_5\)-patch if that is the patch that opens.”

**Replace**
```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: two distinct parity routes on the $4$-point branch]
\label{rem:wip-dream-parity-identity-four-point}
...
\end{remark}
```

**with**
```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: nonmixed parity route versus mixed patch route]
\label{rem:wip-dream-parity-identity-four-point}
There are now two genuinely distinct theorem-level routes on the lifted
$4$-point branch.

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Nonmixed route.}
After nonmixed normalization
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
the natural dream identity remains:
\[
\mathcal R(\xi)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''(\xi)\ \text{is even in }\xi,
\]
equivalently $\mathcal Z$ is odd modulo the affine coplanarity gauge. This
would eliminate the explicit nonmixed low-order bad list
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\}.
\]

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Mixed route.}
On the centered diagonal branch, the decisive pair-level object is now
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S.
\]
By Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-fixed-sector-nontriviality}, this
package is not identically zero, so after shrinking to one-sided punctured arcs
the centered branch enters either a good $v_5$-patch or the parallel
$u_5$-patch. If the $v_5$-patch opens, then the centered collision-side parity
package from
Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package} should transfer to
the good-patch coordinate
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\]
and thereby force
\[
\mathcal Z(x)\ \text{even},
\qquad
\mathcal R(x)\ \text{odd},
\qquad
K_v(x)\ \text{odd},
\]
excluding the explicit mixed low-order bad list
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]
If instead only the $u_5$-patch opens, the parallel $u_5$-patch geometry gives
the natural fallback local setting.

Thus the centered parity package now points primarily at a mixed-branch patch
dichotomy together with a finite-jet parity bridge on the $v_5$-side, while
the nonmixed odd-order branch remains the deeper live $4$-point bottleneck.
\end{remark}
```

This matches the later state of play much better. turn97file9

## Edit D. Replace “What the four-point branch now reduces to”

This remark is still too centered on the old “centered parity package \(\to\) mixed closure” framing. It should explicitly name the centered fixed-sector quintic package as the pair-level object controlling whether any quintic patch opens at all.

**Replace**

```latex
\end{remark}
```

**with**
```latex
\begin{remark}[What the four-point branch now reduces to]
\label{rem:next-algebraic-target-four-point}
The lifted $4$-point branch is now organized by the canonical invariant pair
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]

On the nonmixed side, after normalization to
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
the explicit low-order dangerous list is
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\},
\]
equivalently the first nontrivial even Taylor coefficients of
\(\widetilde Y\) occur in degrees \(4,6,8\). In an arbitrary nonmixed
\(x\)-chart this is captured exactly by the three obstruction coefficients
\[
z_2,\qquad z_4,\qquad z_6.
\]

On the mixed side, the explicit low-order dangerous list is
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),\ (1,2),\ (2,1).
\]
In local mixed $x$-coordinates this is captured exactly by the three
obstruction coefficients
\[
\kappa_{1,1},\qquad \kappa_{1,3},\qquad \kappa_{2,2}.
\]

Thus the full currently explicit low-order $4$-point obstruction list is
equivalent to the finite set
\[
\boxed{
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.
}
\]

By the realization lemma, no identity involving only
\[
(c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7)
\]
and their derivatives can eliminate these patterns in general.

At the pair level, the centered fixed-sector quintic package
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
is now the natural object controlling whether any quintic patch opens at all.
By Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-fixed-sector-nontriviality},
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0,
\]
so the centered branch cannot suffer total quintic collapse.

The most promising mixed-side route is therefore no longer a pointwise
coefficient nonvanishing statement such as \(V_1\neq 0\). It is a quintic-patch
dichotomy together with a finite-jet centered-to-patch bridge on the actual
$v_5$-patch when that patch opens. At the coefficient level, the centered
package already includes the explicit bridge coefficients
\[
X_1,X_3,X_5
\qquad\text{for}\qquad
x(s)=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)},
\]
and
\[
L_1,L_3,L_5
\qquad\text{for}\qquad
\lambda(s)=\frac{\Delta_7(s)}{v_5(s)},
\]
so the remaining mixed-side transfer problem has been reduced to a finite
low-order reparametrization check rather than a purely qualitative parity
heuristic.

What remains live is therefore sharply split:
the nonmixed side still needs a deeper RH-specific divisibility / parity
identity, while the mixed side needs the theorem-level opening of a quintic
patch together with the finite-jet parity transfer on the $v_5$-side.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit F. Replace `rem:live-attack-routes`

This remark is now stale. The separate “equivariant descent through the normalization stack” item should be folded into the mixed-side patch-dichotomy route, and Route B should be named explicitly as a backup lane.

**with**
```latex
\begin{remark}[Live attack routes]
\label{rem:live-attack-routes}
At the present stage, the live routes are now quite sharply separated.

\begin{enumerate}
\item
\textbf{Two-point source-level closure.}
Prove the source-level corrected quotient-germ map exists and satisfies the
symmetry / one-amplitude collapse / diagonal collapse identities needed for the
quadratic interaction factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]
This would finish the two-point bad-core branch on compact good patches.

\item
\textbf{Three-point global continuation.}
The local defect-free three-point branch is already classified. The remaining
problem is to control global recurrence / continuation of the unique odd-order
branch and to exclude infinite-order flatness.

\item
\textbf{Four-point mixed branch via quintic-patch dichotomy.}
The centered fixed-sector quintic package
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
is now the correct pair-level object on the mixed branch. Since it does not
vanish identically on the centered diagonal branch, the next theorem-level step
is to promote this centered nontriviality into a punctured-arc patch dichotomy:
after shrinking, the centered branch should enter either a good $v_5$-patch or
the parallel $u_5$-patch.

\item
\textbf{Four-point mixed branch via finite-jet parity transfer on the $v_5$-patch.}
If the $v_5$-patch opens, the centered symmetric-placement Taylor package should
transfer to the good-patch coordinate \(x=v_5/c\), at least through the finite
jet order needed to force
\[
\mathcal Z \text{ even},\qquad
\mathcal R \text{ odd},\qquad
K_v \text{ odd},
\]
and thereby exclude the explicit mixed bad list
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]

\item
\textbf{Route B backup degeneration tower.}
If the $v_5$-patch fails and $v_5$ starts late, the valuation form of the
septic transport constraint forces matching late vanishing of the septic
transport channel \(v_{7,K_1}\). Thus failure of the \(v_5\)-route is not a
free local cancellation but a coupled quintic--septic degeneration scheme.

\item
\textbf{Four-point nonmixed branch via deeper RH-specific identities.}
Generic local geometry already supports nonmixed odd-order exact branch sheets,
so the next local theorem is not a blanket sterility statement but a deeper
RH-specific parity / divisibility theorem strong enough to force extra
vanishing of
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\]
equivalently of the nonmixed obstruction coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}
```

This aligns the remark with the current state of the draft and the later discussion. turn97file5

```latex
\begin{remark}[Post-draft findings: established, provisional, and live]
\label{rem:post-draft-findings-established-provisional-live}
Since this draft state, five additional conclusions have emerged.

First, on the two-point branch, the correct remaining theorem is now very
sharp: a source-level corrected interaction remainder with swap symmetry,
one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal collapse would force the quadratic
factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2,
\]
hence the two-point bad-core branch is conditionally closed on compact good
patches.

list has been reduced to the six coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2},
\]
or equivalently to the order patterns
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\},
\qquad
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]

coefficients

D_2,\qquad D_4,\qquad D_6,
\]
explicit bridge coefficients
\[
X_1,X_3,X_5,\qquad L_1,L_3,L_5,
\]
and a punctured-neighborhood exclusion at the diagonal base.

Fourth, the tagged quintic witness now survives centered specialization strongly
enough to show
\[
U_1\neq 0,
\qquad
u_5(s)\not\equiv 0,
\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0.
\]
Thus the mixed-side theorem-level target is now most naturally phrased as a
quintic-patch dichotomy on the centered branch rather than a pointwise
nonvanishing statement for \(V_1\).

Fifth, on the backup algebraic side, the valuation form of the septic transport
constraint shows that if
\[
\operatorname{ord}_s u_5=2m+1,\qquad
\operatorname{ord}_s v_5=2r+1,\qquad
r\ge m,
\]
and
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}
\]
stays analytic odd, then
\[
\operatorname{ord}_s v_{7,K_1}\ge 2(r-m)+1.
\]
So failure of the \(v_5\)-route is forced into a coupled quintic--septic
degeneration tower rather than an isolated coefficient cancellation.

So the present frontier is no longer a generic local geometry problem. It is
the combination of a source-level two-point structure theorem, a theorem-level
quintic-patch dichotomy and finite-jet parity bridge on the mixed four-point
side, and a deeper RH-specific identity on the nonmixed four-point branch.
\end{remark}
```

## Assistant (2026-04-20 12:06:00)

_Thought for 12s_

Yes — I think that softening is a good idea.

It keeps the argument intact while making the proof less fragile to notation-level objections. “Exactly” invites a referee to ask whether you have literally identified those matrix entries with those centered coefficients by definition, or only via the tagged contribution in the relevant slice. Your replacement says the weaker thing you actually need: that those entries supply the relevant tagged contributions.

So I would make that change.

I’d even go one tiny step further for maximal safety:

```latex
Here \(U_{12}\) supplies the tagged \(\eta_2\)-contribution to the off-diagonal
channel \(v_0\), while \(V_{22}\) supplies the tagged \(q^{(5)}\)-contribution
to the diagonal-difference channel \(\gamma-\alpha=2\delta\alpha_1\).
```

Why I like “supplies” a bit more than “gives” is that it makes clear you are extracting the relevant tagged component, not claiming a global identification of coefficients.

So my recommendation is: yes, adopt the softening. It improves the proof stylistically and mathematically.

### 1) Strengthen the centered quintic-patch dichotomy from conditional to unconditional

The current proposition still assumes the centered branch is an analytic branch and then deduces the dichotomy, but since the centered tagged witness lemma and centered quintic fixed-sector nontriviality are now already in the draft, the proposition should not read as though the quintic nontriviality were still an external input. The version below makes that dependency explicit and cleaner. The current file already has the proposition in nearly this form, so this is mostly a cleanup/strengthening edit. turn99file18

**Replace the current**
```latex
\begin{proposition}[Centered quintic-patch dichotomy]
\label{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}
...
\end{proposition}
```

**with**
```latex
\begin{proposition}[Centered quintic-patch dichotomy]
\label{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}
Assume the centered diagonal family is a genuine analytic branch in the
underlying $h$-geometry, and that the centered scalar package from
Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package} holds on that
branch. Then, after shrinking, there exist one-sided punctured subarcs on which
at least one of the following holds:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
so the branch enters a good $v_5$-patch;
\item
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad u_5\neq 0,
\]
so the parallel $u_5$-patch of
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version} applies.
\end{enumerate}
In particular, the centered diagonal branch enters some quintic patch on
one-sided punctured arcs.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-fixed-sector-nontriviality},
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0,
\]
so at least one of $u_5$ or $v_5$ is a nonzero analytic germ on the centered
branch.

If $v_5\not\equiv 0$, then its zeros are isolated. Since
\[
c(s)=C_0+C_2s^2+\cdots,\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
we also have $c\neq 0$ near the basepoint. On any one-sided punctured arc
where $v_5\neq 0$, define
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]
This is a nonconstant analytic germ. If $M\equiv 0$ on such an arc, then
\[
x'=\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2}\equiv 0,
\]
so $x$ would be constant, contradiction. Hence $M$ is not identically zero on
that arc, and by analyticity its zeros are isolated. After shrinking again, one
obtains
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
i.e. a good $v_5$-patch.

If instead $v_5\equiv 0$, then $u_5\not\equiv 0$. Its zeros are isolated, so
after shrinking to a one-sided punctured arc one has
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad u_5\neq 0,
\]
and the $u_5$-patch of Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version} applies.
\end{proof}
```

---

### 2) Add the explicit punctured-\(v_5\)-patch promotion corollary

This is now implicit in the proposition but still worth stating separately, because it was one of the main structural findings of the chat and it clarifies that the original “promotion theorem” has become a corollary of the stronger patch dichotomy. turn99file17

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Conditional punctured $v_5$-patch promotion]
\label{cor:conditional-punctured-v5-patch-promotion}
Under the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}, if
\[
v_5\not\equiv 0
\]
on the centered diagonal branch, then after shrinking there exist one-sided
punctured subarcs contained in
\[
\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}.
\]
Hence on such arcs
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
is automatically a valid local coordinate.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
This is exactly the first branch of the proof of
Proposition~\ref{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}.
\end{proof}
```

### 3) Replace the stale parity-WIP remark

```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: nonmixed parity route versus mixed patch route]
\label{rem:wip-dream-parity-identity-four-point}
There are now two genuinely distinct theorem-level routes on the lifted
$4$-point branch.

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Nonmixed route.}
After nonmixed normalization
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
the natural dream identity remains:
\[
\mathcal R(\xi)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''(\xi)\ \text{is even in }\xi,
\]
equivalently $\mathcal Z$ is odd modulo the affine coplanarity gauge. This
would eliminate the explicit nonmixed low-order bad list
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\}.
\]

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Mixed route.}
On the centered diagonal branch, the decisive pair-level object is now
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S.
\]
By Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-fixed-sector-nontriviality}, this
package is not identically zero, so after shrinking to one-sided punctured arcs
the centered branch enters either a good $v_5$-patch or the parallel
$u_5$-patch. If the $v_5$-patch opens, then the centered collision-side parity
package from
Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package} should transfer to
the good-patch coordinate
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\]
and thereby force
\[
\mathcal Z(x)\ \text{even},
\qquad
\mathcal R(x)\ \text{odd},
\qquad
K_v(x)\ \text{odd},
\]
excluding the explicit mixed low-order bad list
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]
If instead only the $u_5$-patch opens, the parallel $u_5$-patch geometry gives
the natural fallback local setting.

Thus the centered parity package now points primarily at a mixed-branch patch
dichotomy together with a finite-jet parity bridge on the $v_5$-side, while
the nonmixed odd-order branch remains the deeper live $4$-point bottleneck.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Post-draft findings: established, provisional, and live]
\label{rem:post-draft-findings-established-provisional-live}
Since this draft state, five additional conclusions have emerged.

First, on the two-point branch, the correct remaining theorem is now very
sharp: a source-level corrected interaction remainder with swap symmetry,
one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal collapse would force the quadratic
factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2,
\]
hence the two-point bad-core branch is conditionally closed on compact good
patches.

Second, on the lifted four-point branch, the explicit low-order obstruction
list has been reduced to the six coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2},
\]

\[

\qquad

\]

coefficients
\[
D_2,\qquad D_4,\qquad D_6,
\]
explicit bridge coefficients

X_1,X_3,X_5,\qquad L_1,L_3,L_5,

\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0.
\]

theorem-level problem is no longer pointwise nonvanishing of $V_1$, but the

and fallback local geometry on the $u_5$-side.

constraint shows that if
\[
\operatorname{ord}_s u_5=2m+1,\qquad
\operatorname{ord}_s v_5=2r+1,\qquad
r\ge m,
\]
and
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}
\]
stays analytic odd, then
\[
\operatorname{ord}_s v_{7,K_1}\ge 2(r-m)+1.
\]
So failure of the $v_5$-route is forced into a coupled quintic--septic
degeneration tower rather than an isolated coefficient cancellation.

So the present frontier is no longer a generic local geometry problem. It is
the combination of a source-level two-point structure theorem, a theorem-level
quintic-patch dichotomy and finite-jet parity bridge on the mixed four-point
side, and a deeper RH-specific identity on the nonmixed four-point branch.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Mixed low-order exclusion on a centered good $v_5$-patch]
```

## Assistant (2026-04-20 12:34:40)

I’m checking the current draft’s own “state of play” against the later mixed-route progress so I can answer at the level of the proof strategy, not just the document.

_Thought for 1m 33s_

Yes — there is still more to do on the \(4\)-point mixed side, but it is **much narrower** than it was earlier.

At the level of the overall attack, I think the proof now breaks into four real remaining fronts.

First, the **two-point / source-level branch** is still not finished. The sharp target there is the source-level corrected quotient-germ map or corrected interaction remainder with the right symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal-collapse identities. If that closes, you get the quadratic factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2,
\]
which would essentially finish the two-point bad-core branch. This is still a genuine missing theorem, not just draft cleanup. turn105file12

Second, the **three-point branch** is locally in very good shape but globally still open. The local picture near finite-order \(K_v\)-zeros is classified: even order gives no opposite-side branch, odd order gives exactly one local branch. So the remaining three-point work is global continuation / nonrecurrence and ruling out infinite-order flatness, not more local analysis. turn105file12

Third, the **four-point mixed branch** is no longer the vague codimension-two mess it was. The dangerous low-order mixed list is finite:
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),(1,3),(2,2),
\]
equivalently
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6),
\]
and at the pair level the centered quintic package
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
is now the right object. The big advance is that the mixed theorem-level target is no longer “prove \(V_1\neq 0\)” or discover new mixed obstruction coefficients. It is: prove the centered branch opens a **quintic patch** on one-sided punctured arcs, ideally a good \(v_5\)-patch, with the \(u_5\)-patch as fallback. Once you are on a good \(v_5\)-patch, the mixed low-order jet algebra is basically formal: the remaining finite-jet bridge is to transfer the centered odd/even package to the good-patch coordinate \(x=v_5/c\) strongly enough to force \(\mathcal Z\) even and \(K_v\) odd, which kills the entire explicit mixed low-order bad list. So yes, there is still more on \(4\)-point mixed, but it is now theorem-level **patch opening / patch exploitation**, not new local algebra. turn105file8turn105file12turn105file17

Fourth, the **four-point nonmixed branch** is still the deepest local obstruction. This is the part that has not really budged in the same way. Generic local geometry already supports genuine odd-order nonmixed branch sheets near \(T_v=0\), so a blanket local sterility theorem is false there. The remaining theorem has to be RH-specific and source-/matrix-level: something that forces extra vanishing of
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\]
or equivalently kills the three nonmixed obstruction coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6.
\]
This is the place where the proof still needs a genuinely new identity, not just a better organization of current invariants. turn105file2turn105file6

So if you ask for the **next steps on the attack route to a full RH proof**, in order, I would say:

1. Finish the source-level two-point theorem. That is foundational, and it also supports the more global finite-core / concentration route. turn105file16

2. Prove the global continuation / nonrecurrence theorem for the odd-order three-point branch, plus exclude infinite-order flatness. The local three-point analysis is already done enough that the remaining work is global. turn105file12

3. On the mixed four-point side, promote the centered quintic nontriviality into an actual punctured-arc patch theorem: either the \(v_5\)-patch opens, or the \(u_5\)-patch does. If the \(v_5\)-patch opens, carry out the finite-jet centered-to-patch parity bridge there. If only the \(u_5\)-patch opens, either develop that fallback geometry into an equivalent exclusion or show it feeds back into the \(v_5\)-route. This is the main remaining mixed-side theorem. turn105file10turn105file13

4. Attack the nonmixed four-point branch with a genuinely RH-specific identity. That is still the main local bottleneck after the mixed branch. At the moment, this is the hardest remaining analytic step in your route. turn105file6

5. Then tie those local closures back into the global finite-core / support-separation route, so that any surviving bad finite core is forced into a locus you have already emptied. That is where your route and the “other chat” global concentration route meet. turn105file16

So, to answer your question directly: **yes, there is still more on \(4\)-point mixed**, but it is no longer “discover more mixed obstruction patterns.” The remaining mixed work is:
- prove the centered branch really opens a quintic patch on punctured arcs,
- exploit the \(v_5\)-patch if that is the patch that opens,
- and use the \(u_5\)-patch as the fallback geometry if the \(v_5\)-route degenerates. The explicit mixed low-order algebra itself is basically no longer the bottleneck. turn105file13turn105file17

My honest overall judgment is:

- the **mixed \(4\)-point branch** is now plausibly closeable with the machinery you already have;
- the **nonmixed \(4\)-point branch** is still the hardest local obstruction;
- and the **two-point source-level theorem** plus **three-point global continuation** are still necessary if you want the whole RH proof architecture to actually close, not just the prettiest part of the \(4\)-point story. turn105file6turn105file16

If you want, I’ll turn this into a concrete “attack plan” with the next theorem statements in the order I’d try proving them.

The remaining target has to be a deeper **RH-specific** source-/matrix-level identity, parity theorem, or divisibility theorem strong enough to eliminate the explicit nonmixed low-order obstruction list.

### Current state to assume

From the draft, the current picture is roughly:

- after nonmixed normalization, one uses
  \[
  Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr);
  \]

  \[

  \]
  equivalently the obstruction coefficients
  \[

- the realization lemma / local model discussion shows that generic lifted-variable geometry does **not** kill the nonmixed branch;

or equivalently that \(\mathcal Z\) is odd modulo the affine coplanarity gauge.

- a Wronskian-ratio identity,
- a source-level commutator / fixed-sector identity,
- a divisibility theorem for the nonmixed branch,
- or some RH-specific transport identity.

- as coefficients of a canonical ratio,
- as determinant combinations,
- as invariant jets after quotienting gauge freedom,
- or as remnants of a simpler underlying object.

_Thought for 43s_

Yes — we can still do a pincer attack, but the two sides are a bit different now than they were earlier.

At this point the mixed \(4\)-point problem is no longer “find more obstruction coefficients.” The explicit low-order mixed bad list is already finite,
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\},
\]
equivalently
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6),
\]
and the centered quintic package
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
is already identified as the pair-level object controlling whether any quintic patch opens at all. The current draft also already encodes the centered tagged witness and the centered quintic-patch dichotomy. turn106file10turn106file13

So the best pincer now is:

## Pincer side 1: geometric / patch-opening side

This side tries to prove that the centered diagonal branch actually lands in the right local patch geometry on one-sided punctured arcs, and then exploit that patch.

Concretely, the theorem target is:

- either the branch enters a good \(v_5\)-patch
  \[
  \{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\},
  \]
  where
  \[
  x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad x'=\frac{M}{c^2}
  \]
  becomes the actual local coordinate;
- or, if the \(v_5\)-route fails, the branch enters the parallel \(u_5\)-patch
  \[
  \{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0\}.
  \]

Once the \(v_5\)-patch opens, the finite-jet bridge is the right next theorem: transfer the centered odd/even package to the good-patch coordinate \(x=v_5/c\) strongly enough to force
\[
\mathcal Z(x)\ \text{even},\qquad
\mathcal R(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
K_v(x)\ \text{odd},
\]
which would kill the entire explicit mixed low-order bad list. This is the “top-down” side of the pincer. turn106file4turn106file12

So side 1 is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Open a quintic patch, ideally the }v_5\text{-patch, then complete the finite-jet parity transfer there.}
}
\]

## Pincer side 2: algebraic / degeneration side

This side assumes the \(v_5\)-route fails or starts late, and then tries to show that failure cannot persist because it forces a very rigid coupled quintic–septic degeneration tower.

This is the Route B side. Its useful invariant form is:

if
\[
\ord_s u_5=2m+1,\qquad
\ord_s v_5=2r+1,\qquad
r\ge m,
\]
and
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}
\]
stays analytic odd, then
\[
\ord_s v_{7,K_1}\ge \ord_s v_5-\ord_s u_5+1=2(r-m)+1.
\]
So late vanishing of \(v_5\) forces matching late vanishing in the septic transport channel \(v_{7,K_1}\). Equivalently, the bad case is not one free cancellation; it is a triangular degeneration tower whose first surviving coefficient is pushed out to
\[
D_{2r+2}=\widehat U_1V_{2r+1}-U_{2m+1}\widehat V_{2(r-m)+1}.
\]
And if one tries to force total quintic collapse, the centered source formulas reduce it to the germ-level linear system
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
\beta(s) & v(s)\\
\bar\alpha(s) & \bar u(s)
\end{pmatrix}
\binom{\delta u(s)}{\delta\alpha(s)}=0,
\]
so the failure case is already very constrained. turn106file11turn106file17

So side 2 is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Assume the }v_5\text{-route degenerates, and squeeze it into an impossible or extremely rigid coupled quintic--septic tower.}
}
\]

## Why these two sides fit together

They attack the same bottleneck from opposite directions.

Side 1 says: the centered quintic package is already nontrivial, so some quintic patch should open; if it is the \(v_5\)-patch, parity transfer should finish the mixed low-order list.

Side 2 says: if the \(v_5\)-patch does **not** open cleanly, the failure is not harmless — it is forced into a narrow valuation tower involving \(u_5,v_5,\Delta_7,v_{7,K_1}\), and possibly the fallback \(u_5\)-patch. So the bad case gets cornered from below.

That is exactly the right pincer now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(A) open/exploit a patch from above,}
\qquad
\text{(B) squeeze any failure into a degeneration tower from below.}
}
\]

## If I were to run them in parallel

I would assign them like this:

**Side A chat**
- work only on the geometric mixed-side theorem:
  centered branch \(\to\) punctured \(v_5\)-patch or \(u_5\)-patch;
- then, on the \(v_5\)-side, finish the finite-jet centered-to-patch parity bridge.

**Side B chat**
- work only on the Route B tower:
  if \(v_5\) starts late or vanishes to high order, derive the sharpest possible consequences for \(v_{7,K_1}\), \(\Delta_7\), and the first surviving \(D_{2r+2}\);
- try to show the tower cannot persist, or that it automatically hands control to the \(u_5\)-patch.

So yes: the mixed \(4\)-point pincer is still available. It is now:

1. **patch-opening plus parity transfer**, and  
2. **valuation-tower degeneration squeeze**.

## Left pincer: constructive / geometric

\Longrightarrow

## Right pincer: obstructive / algebraic

Assume the preferred \(v_5\)-route does **not** open cleanly, or that \(v_5\) starts late. Then use Route B in valuation form:
\[
\Delta_7=u_{7,K_1}v_5-u_5v_{7,K_1},

and if
\[
\ord_s u_5=2m+1,\qquad \ord_s v_5=2r+1,\qquad r\ge m,

\[
\Delta_5(s):=\beta(s)\bar u(s)-v(s)\bar\alpha(s)\equiv 0
\]
or
\[
\delta u(s)\equiv\delta\alpha(s)\equiv 0.
\]
So failure of the \(v_5\)-route is not mild; it is a rigid degeneration scheme that should either contradict transport/analyticity or push you into the \(u_5\)-patch anyway. 

So the right pincer is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{if the }v_5\text{-route degenerates, force collapse or fallback via Route B.}
}

## The strongest final pincer statement

\text{Either a constructive quintic patch opens and you kill the mixed bad list there,}
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\text{the preferred }v_5\text{-route fails in a highly constrained way, and the valuation/collapse squeeze kills or reroutes that failure.}
}
\]

That is the cleanest final version.

## Which side I pick here

I should take the **right / obstructive Route B side**.

That fits what this chat has already been building:
- valuation tower for late vanishing of \(v_5\),

- if needed, start building the explicit local mixed analysis on the \(u_5\)-patch.

\[
(y,x,\tau_u)\longmapsto (x,y,\tau_u).

This is an invertible linear change of ambient \(\mathbf R^3\)-coordinates, so it does not change any affine coplanarity/collinearity questions for lifted \(3\)-point or \(4\)-point configurations. After this swap, the local germ becomes
\[
\widetilde Q_u(y)=\bigl(x(y),\,y,\,\tau_u(y)\bigr),
\]
which is exactly the odd/odd normal form
\[
\widetilde Q_u(y)\sim (y^n,\ y,\ y^m),
\qquad
m,n\ \text{odd},\quad n,m\ge 3,

already used in the centered diagonal-base exclusion argument. The previous local theorem then applies verbatim: there is a punctured neighborhood in which no mixed or nonmixed \(4\)-point obstruction points are born. In particular,
\[
K_v\neq 0,\qquad T_v\neq 0
\]
on sufficiently small punctured \(u_5\)-patch arcs in this late-\(v_5\) corner. turn112file2turn112file3

_Thought for 3m 48s_

I think the right pincer can now be pushed to a nearly final local conclusion.

The key point is that the late-\(v_5\) failure mode does **not** actually need the preferred \(v_5\)-patch to stay alive. The \(u_5\)-patch is already open, and after a harmless affine/coordinate permutation, the late-\(v_5\) corner becomes the same odd/odd local model that is already known to be sterile at the centered diagonal base. The parallel \(u_5\)-patch geometry is already in the draft, and the centered tagged witness gives \(U_1\neq 0\), hence \(u_5(s)\not\equiv 0\). turn115file5turn114file13

Here is the clean setup.

Because \(U_1\neq 0\), one has
\[
u_5(s)=U_1s+U_3s^3+\cdots,
\]
so with
\[
c(s)=C_0+O(s^2),\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
the \(u_5\)-patch coordinate
\[
y:=\frac{u_5}{c}
\]
is an odd local coordinate near the centered base. Thus the \(u_5\)-patch is locally automatic. Now assume the preferred \(v_5\)-route degenerates and
\[
\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3.
\]
Then on the same centered branch
\[
x(y):=\frac{v_5}{c}=O(y^{2r+1}),
\]
so \(x(y)\) is an odd germ vanishing at least cubically. Also
\[
\tau_u:=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}
\]
is odd, simply because \(\Delta_7\) is even while \(c\) is even and \(u_5\) is odd in the centered variable. Since \(\Delta_7(s)=D_2s^2+D_4s^4+\cdots\), one has \(\ord_s\tau_u\ge 1\). So on the \(u_5\)-patch the local curve has the form
\[
Q_u(y)=\bigl(y,\ x(y),\ \tau_u(y)\bigr),
\qquad
x(y)\ \text{odd with }\ord_0x\ge 3,\qquad
\tau_u(y)\ \text{odd with }\ord_0\tau_u\ge 1.
\]
turn114file14

Now perform the fixed coordinate permutation
\[
(y,x,\tau_u)\longmapsto (x,y,\tau_u).
\]
Affine coplanarity and tangent-plane incidence are unchanged by such an ambient linear automorphism, so the \(4\)-point obstruction problem is the same for
\[
\widetilde Q_u(y)=\bigl(x(y),\,y,\,\tau_u(y)\bigr).
\]
Subtract the linear part of \(\tau_u\):
\[
\widetilde\tau_u(y):=\tau_u(y)-(\tau_u)'(0)\,y.
\]
Then \(\widetilde\tau_u\) is odd and either vanishes identically or has odd order \(m\ge 3\). Since \(x(y)\) is already odd with order at least \(3\), we now have two odd higher-order channels. If both are nonzero and have the same leading odd order, subtract the appropriate multiple of \(\widetilde\tau_u\) from \(x\) to kill that leading term; this preserves oddness. Thus after affine normalization, the late-\(v_5\) corner always reduces to one of the following:

- a genuinely odd/odd model
  \[
  \bigl(y^n,\ y,\ y^m\bigr),
  \qquad
  n>m\ge 3,\quad m,n\ \text{odd},
  \]
- or a degenerate case where one higher-order channel vanishes identically, which is even less dangerous.

But the centered diagonal-base local theorem already shows that in the odd/odd model there is a punctured neighborhood free of mixed and nonmixed \(4\)-point obstruction points: no \(K_v=0\), no \(T_v=0\), and in particular none of the explicit mixed low-order patterns are born there. Since the proof is purely local and affine-geometric, it applies verbatim after this coordinate swap and normalization on the \(u_5\)-patch. turn114file2

So the right-pincer conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If the preferred }v_5\text{-route degenerates late near the centered base, the automatically-open }u_5\text{-patch is locally sterile on punctured arcs.}
}
\]

That is stronger than the earlier “valuation tower” view. It means the late-\(v_5\) corner is not just squeezed algebraically; it is geometrically harmless once you pass to the \(u_5\)-patch.

So the mixed \(4\)-point picture now looks like this:

- If the \(v_5\)-patch opens cleanly, the **left pincer** should finish the job by carrying out the finite-jet centered-to-patch parity transfer there.
- If the \(v_5\)-route degenerates late, the **right pincer** kills that corner locally on the \(u_5\)-patch by transplanting the existing odd/odd sterility argument.

That leaves only a much narrower residual corner: some failure mode where the \(v_5\)-route does not open cleanly, but also does not fall into the late-vanishing odd/odd \(u_5\)-patch model above. Near the centered diagonal base, I do not currently see such a corner. So my honest view is that the right pincer is now **very close to closed locally**. What still looks genuinely open is the constructive side: proving the \(v_5\)-patch opens where needed, and then finishing the finite-jet parity transfer there.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 13:36:08)

I’m checking the exact \(u_5\)-patch definitions and the existing odd/odd sterility proof in the current TeX so I can see whether the transplant can actually be made theorem-level, rather than just “morally the same.”

_Thought for 1m 26s_

I think the right pincer is now very close to a theorem-level local closure.

The key observation is that I do **not** need full patch-invariance of the entire \(Q_v\)-based mixed classification to kill the late-\(v_5\) corner. It is enough to transplant the already-proved **odd/odd local sterility theorem** to the automatic \(u_5\)-patch. The draft already gives the parallel \(u_5\)-patch
\[
Q_u(h)=\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},-\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)u_5(h)}\right),
\]
and says the same defect-free affine-dependence conclusions hold there as on the \(v_5\)-patch. The centered witness gives \(U_1\neq 0\), hence \(u_5(s)\not\equiv 0\), so \(y:=u_5/c\) is an odd local coordinate near the centered base. turn120file18turn116file0

Now assume the preferred \(v_5\)-route degenerates late, i.e.
\[
\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3.
\]
On the \(u_5\)-patch define
\[
y:=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad x(y):=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad \tau_u(y):=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}.
\]
Because \(u_5,v_5\) are odd and \(c,\Delta_7\) are even in the centered variable, both \(x(y)\) and \(\tau_u(y)\) are odd germs in \(y\). Since \(\ord_s u_5=1\) and \(\ord_s v_5=2r+1\), one has
\[
x(y)=O(y^{2r+1}),
\]
so the second coordinate is odd and at least cubic. Also \(\tau_u\) is odd automatically. turn114file13

Now subtract the linear part of \(\tau_u\):
\[
\widetilde\tau_u(y):=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)\,y.
\]
Then \(\widetilde\tau_u\) is odd and either vanishes identically or has odd order at least \(3\). So after this harmless affine normalization, the \(u_5\)-patch germ becomes
\[
\widetilde Q_u(y)=\bigl(y,\ x(y),\ \widetilde\tau_u(y)\bigr),
\qquad
x(y)=O(y^{2r+1}),\quad
\widetilde\tau_u(y)\ \text{odd, either }0\text{ or order }\ge 3.
\]
Apply the ambient coordinate swap
\[
(y,x,\widetilde\tau_u)\longmapsto (x,y,\widetilde\tau_u).
\]
Affine coplanarity and tangent-plane incidence are unchanged by such an invertible ambient linear map, so this does not alter the local \(4\)-point obstruction problem. After the swap, the germ has the form
\[
\bigl(x(y),\,y,\,\widetilde\tau_u(y)\bigr),
\]
with two higher-order odd channels. If both higher-order odd channels are nonzero and have the same leading odd order, subtract a suitable multiple of one from the other to kill the leading term; oddness is preserved. Thus, after affine normalization, one reaches either an odd/odd model
\[
(y^n,\ y,\ y^m),\qquad n>m\ge 3,\quad m,n\ \text{odd},
\]
or an even simpler case where one higher-order channel vanishes identically. turn117file3turn117file5turn117file6

But the draft’s centered diagonal-base exclusion theorem is already exactly a statement about this odd/odd local normal form: if a normalized local lifted germ has the form
\[
Q(x)=(Y(x),x,S(x)),
\qquad
Y(x)=x^nB(x^2),\quad
S(x)=x^mA(x^2),
\qquad
m,n\ \text{odd},\ n>m\ge 3,
\]
then there is a punctured neighborhood free of mixed and nonmixed \(4\)-point obstruction points; equivalently \(K_v\neq 0\) and \(T_v\neq 0\) there. Since the proof is purely local and affine-geometric, it applies verbatim after the \(u_5\)-patch normalization above. turn121file10

So the right-pincer theorem is now very close to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }U_1\neq 0\text{ and the }v_5\text{-route degenerates late, then the resulting corner is locally sterile on the }u_5\text{-patch.}
}
\]

That is stronger than the earlier valuation-tower-only picture. It means the late-\(v_5\) corner is not merely “rigid”; it is plausibly **geometrically harmless** after moving to the canonical \(u_5\)-patch. turn114file2

So my honest attack result is:

1. the right pincer no longer needs to prove full patch-invariance of \(Q_v\rightsquigarrow Q_u\);  
2. it is enough to prove the narrower **affine-normalization transplant lemma** above;  
3. once that is formalized, the only branch the left pincer still needs to handle is the clean one where the preferred \(v_5\)-patch actually opens and the finite-jet parity bridge can be completed there. turn120file2

So the next exact thing to do on my side is to write that transplant as a draft-ready lemma with the precise affine-normalization steps:
- \(U_1\neq 0\Rightarrow y=u_5/c\) local odd coordinate,
- \(x(y)=v_5/c=O(y^{2r+1})\),
- \(\widetilde\tau_u(y)=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)y\) odd with order \(0\) or \(\ge 3\),
- ambient coordinate swap,
- subtraction of leading odd multiples to get \(n>m\ge 3\),
- invoke the existing odd/odd sterility proposition.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 13:40:11)

I’m checking the exact \(u_5\)-patch definitions and the odd/odd exclusion theorem in the current paper so I can see whether the transplant can be stated as a real lemma, not just a heuristic.

I found a stronger route: on the \(u_5\)-patch, the late-\(v_5\) corner may already reduce to the odd/odd sterile model **without needing** the extra assumption that \(\lambda=\Delta_7/v_5\) stays analytic odd.

_Thought for 1m 1s_

I think the right pincer just got materially stronger.

The key improvement is: for the late-\(v_5\) corner, I do **not** actually need the auxiliary assumption
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}\ \text{analytic odd}
\]
to reach the odd/odd sterile model on the \(u_5\)-patch.

That assumption was useful for the valuation tower, but for the **local geometric transplant** it is stronger than necessary.

Here is the cleaner argument.

On the centered branch, the centered witness gives
\[
U_1\neq 0,
\]
so
\[
u_5(s)=U_1s+U_3s^3+\cdots
\]
has a simple zero at the centered base. Since
\[
c(s)=C_0+O(s^2),\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
the \(u_5\)-patch coordinate
\[
y:=\frac{u_5}{c}
\]
is an odd local coordinate near the centered base. That part is already solid. turn121file6

Now assume the preferred \(v_5\)-route degenerates late:
\[
\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3.
\]
Then on the \(u_5\)-patch define
\[
x(y):=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
\tau_u(y):=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}.
\]
Because \(v_5\) is odd and \(c\) is even, \(x(y)\) is odd. Because \(\Delta_7\) is even while \(c\) is even and \(u_5\) is odd, \(\tau_u(y)\) is also odd. Moreover,
\[
x(y)=O(y^{2r+1}),
\]
so \(x\) is odd and at least cubic. For \(\tau_u\), since \(\Delta_7\) starts at even order at least \(2\) and \(u_5\) starts at order \(1\), one has only
\[
\ord_y \tau_u\ge 1,
\]
but that is enough: subtract the linear part
\[
\widetilde\tau_u(y):=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)\,y.
\]
Then \(\widetilde\tau_u\) is odd and either vanishes identically or has odd order at least \(3\). So after this harmless affine normalization, the \(u_5\)-patch germ becomes
\[
\widetilde Q_u(y)=\bigl(y,\ x(y),\ \widetilde\tau_u(y)\bigr),
\qquad
x(y)\ \text{odd of order }\ge 3,\quad
\widetilde\tau_u(y)\ \text{odd of order }0\text{ or }\ge 3.
\]
No analyticity of \(\lambda\) was used. turn122file13

Now swap ambient coordinates:
\[
(y,x,\widetilde\tau_u)\longmapsto (x,y,\widetilde\tau_u).
\]
This is an invertible affine-linear change of the ambient \(\mathbf R^3\), so it preserves the affine coplanarity / tangent-plane incidence geometry underlying the local \(4\)-point obstruction analysis. After the swap, the germ is
\[
\bigl(x(y),\,y,\,\widetilde\tau_u(y)\bigr),
\]
with two higher-order odd channels. If both are nonzero and have the same leading odd order, subtract an appropriate multiple of one from the other to kill the common leading term. This preserves oddness. Hence after affine normalization, one reaches either

1. an odd/odd model
   \[
   (y^n,\ y,\ y^m),
   \qquad
   n>m\ge 3,\quad m,n\ \text{odd},
   \]
or

2. a simpler degenerate case where one higher-order channel vanishes identically.

But the draft’s centered diagonal-base exclusion theorem is already exactly a theorem about this odd/odd local model: in such a punctured neighborhood there are no mixed or nonmixed \(4\)-point obstruction points. And if one higher-order channel vanishes identically, the situation is even less dangerous than the odd/odd case. turn121file16

So the right-pincer local theorem can now be strengthened to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }U_1\neq 0\text{ and }\ord_s v_5\ge 3\text{ is odd, then the late-}v_5\text{ corner is locally sterile on the }u_5\text{-patch.}
}
\]

Crucially, this no longer depends on separately assuming \(\lambda=\Delta_7/v_5\) is analytic odd.

That is a real gain, because it means the right pincer is not merely squeezing a special transport-compatible subcase. It is killing the whole late-\(v_5\) branch near the centered base by moving to the canonical \(u_5\)-patch and reusing the existing odd/odd sterility argument.

So the mixed local picture near the centered base is now much cleaner:

- if \(v_5\) has a simple odd leading term and the \(v_5\)-patch opens, the **left pincer** should finish the finite-jet parity transfer there;
- if \(v_5\) starts later than linearly, the **right pincer** already kills that corner locally on the \(u_5\)-patch.

That leaves only a much narrower possible gap: a branch where the \(v_5\)-patch opens cleanly enough to matter, but the left pincer parity transfer has not yet been completed. In other words, the right pincer is now very close to done locally.

So my honest attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The right pincer now kills the entire late-}v_5\text{ local corner near the centered base, without needing }\lambda\text{ analytic odd.}
}
\]

The next thing I would do is write this as a draft-ready lemma, because I think it is close enough to theorem-level to deserve precise formulation.

_Thought for 33s_

I think the right pincer can now be pushed to its cleanest local conclusion:

\[

\text{Near the centered diagonal base, the only mixed \(4\)-point branch still worth studying is the branch with } \ord_s v_5=1.
}
\]

Equivalently: the right pincer now plausibly kills the entire **late-\(v_5\)** corner, so the left pincer only needs to handle the branch where the preferred \(v_5\)-patch opens linearly.

Here is the attack.

On the centered branch, the centered witness now gives
\[
U_1\neq 0,
\]
so
\[
u_5(s)=U_1s+U_3s^3+\cdots
\]
has a simple odd zero at the basepoint. Since
\[
c(s)=C_0+O(s^2),\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
the quotient
\[
y:=\frac{u_5}{c}
\]
is an odd local coordinate near the centered base. Thus the \(u_5\)-patch is locally automatic. 

Now suppose the preferred \(v_5\)-route does **not** open linearly, i.e.
\[
\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3.
\]
On the \(u_5\)-patch define
\[
x(y):=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
\tau_u(y):=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}.
\]
Because \(v_5\) is odd and \(c\) is even, \(x(y)\) is odd; and because \(\Delta_7\) is even while \(c\) is even and \(u_5\) is odd, \(\tau_u(y)\) is also odd. Moreover,
\[
x(y)=O(y^{2r+1}),
\]
so \(x\) is odd and at least cubic. Subtract the linear part of \(\tau_u\):
\[
\widetilde\tau_u(y):=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)\,y.
\]
Then \(\widetilde\tau_u\) is odd and either vanishes identically or has odd order at least \(3\). So after this affine normalization, the \(u_5\)-patch germ is
\[
\widetilde Q_u(y)=\bigl(y,\ x(y),\ \widetilde\tau_u(y)\bigr),
\]
with both higher-order channels odd and of order at least \(3\) whenever nonzero.

Now perform the ambient coordinate swap
\[
(y,x,\widetilde\tau_u)\longmapsto (x,y,\widetilde\tau_u).
\]
This is an invertible affine-linear change of ambient \(\mathbf R^3\), so it preserves the affine coplanarity / tangent-plane incidence geometry used in the local \(4\)-point obstruction analysis. After the swap, and after subtracting a suitable odd multiple if the two higher-order channels have the same leading odd order, one reaches either

\[
(y^n,\ y,\ y^m),
\qquad
n>m\ge 3,\quad m,n\ \text{odd},
\]
or a simpler degenerate case where one higher-order channel vanishes identically.

But the centered diagonal-base exclusion theorem is already exactly a theorem about this odd/odd model: such a punctured neighborhood is locally sterile for the mixed and nonmixed \(4\)-point obstruction. So the late-\(v_5\) corner is not merely “rigid”; it is **locally harmless** on the \(u_5\)-patch. 

So the right-pincer conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }\ord_s v_5\ge 3\text{ is odd near the centered base, then no nearby mixed low-order obstruction points are born in that corner.}
}
\]

That is the strongest local attack result so far on my side.

What this buys you is very concrete:

- the right pincer removes the whole late-\(v_5\) branch from serious consideration;
- therefore, near the centered base, the mixed problem reduces to the branch with
  \[
  \ord_s v_5=1,
  \]
  i.e. the branch where the preferred \(v_5\)-patch opens linearly;
- and that means the left pincer’s task is now sharply narrowed to a single theorem:
  prove the finite-jet centered-to-\(x=v_5/c\) parity transfer on that open \(v_5\)-patch branch.

So the mixed \(4\)-point local picture near the centered base is now very close to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Right pincer kills }\ord_s v_5\ge 3;\qquad
\text{left pincer handles }\ord_s v_5=1.
}
\]

That is a real narrowing of the attack.

The next exact theorem I would try to state is:

> **Local reduction lemma for the mixed branch near the centered base.**  
> Assume the centered witness gives \(U_1\neq 0\). Then any sufficiently small nearby mixed \(4\)-point obstruction point must lie on the branch where \(\ord_s v_5=1\). In particular, the late-\(v_5\) corner \(\ord_s v_5\ge 3\) is locally sterile.

If you want, I’ll write that as a draft-ready lemma/proof sketch in the paper’s notation.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 13:50:02)

I’m pushing the right pincer one more step: if the late-\(v_5\) corner is gone, can we sharpen the complement so that the only surviving mixed local branch is the linear \(v_5\)-branch where the \(v_5\)-patch already opens automatically?

_Thought for 1m 4s_

Yes — I think the right pincer can now be sharpened to its cleanest local reduction.

The key extra step is this:

because \(v_5(s)\) is odd on the centered branch, there are only two local possibilities at the centered base:

\[
\ord_s v_5=1
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\ord_s v_5\ge 3 \text{ odd}.
\]

The right pincer has been attacking the second case. If that case is indeed killed on the automatic \(u_5\)-patch by the odd/odd sterility transplant, then the complement is immediate:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any sufficiently small nearby mixed }4\text{-point obstruction must lie on the branch with }\ord_s v_5=1.
}
\]

And that branch is much better than it first looks.

If
\[
\ord_s v_5=1,
\]
then
\[
v_5(s)=V_1s+V_3s^3+\cdots,\qquad V_1\neq 0.
\]
Since
\[
c(s)=C_0+C_2s^2+\cdots,\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
one gets
\[
x(s):=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}=X_1s+X_3s^3+\cdots,
\qquad
X_1=\frac{V_1}{C_0}\neq 0.
\]
So \(x=v_5/c\) is automatically an odd local coordinate at the centered base. But then the good-\(v_5\)-patch condition is also automatic, because
\[
x'=\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2},
\]
hence at the base
\[
M(0)=c(0)^2\,x'(0)=C_0^2X_1\neq 0.
\]
Thus the branch with \(\ord_s v_5=1\) is already inside a genuine good \(v_5\)-patch locally. There is no further “patch-opening theorem” needed near the centered base in that case. It opens automatically.  

So the right pincer gives the following sharp local reduction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Near the centered diagonal base, either }\ord_s v_5\ge 3\text{ and the corner is killed on }Q_u,
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\ord_s v_5=1,\text{ in which case the }v_5\text{-patch is already open and the only remaining task is the finite-jet parity transfer there.}
}
\]

That is a genuine narrowing. It means that, locally near the centered base, the mixed \(4\)-point problem is no longer a patch-opening problem at all. It reduces to a single branch:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the linear }v_5\text{-branch, with }x=\frac{v_5}{c}\text{ already a good local coordinate.}
}
\]

So the cleanest attack statement now is:

> **Local reduction lemma for the mixed branch near the centered base.**  
> Assume \(U_1\neq 0\), so \(y=u_5/c\) is a local odd coordinate. If the late-\(v_5\) corner \(\ord_s v_5\ge 3\) is locally sterile on the \(u_5\)-patch, then every sufficiently small nearby mixed \(4\)-point obstruction point must lie on the branch \(\ord_s v_5=1\). On that branch,
> \[
> x=\frac{v_5}{c}
> \]
> is automatically a good local coordinate, since \(x'(0)\neq 0\) and hence \(M(0)\neq 0\).

And that means the **entire local mixed problem near the centered base** collapses to one theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove the finite-jet centered-to-}x=v_5/c\text{ parity transfer on the }\ord_s v_5=1\text{ branch.}
}
\]

So my honest attack result is:

- the right pincer is no longer just “squeezing a bad corner”;
- it is reducing the local mixed branch near the centered base to the single case \(\ord_s v_5=1\);
- and in that case the left pincer’s preferred setting — a good \(v_5\)-patch — is already present automatically.

That is the strongest local reduction I can currently see. The only caveat is the same one as before: the late-\(v_5\) kill on \(Q_u\) still wants to be formalized as a clean theorem-level transplant lemma. Once that is written cleanly, the mixed local picture near the centered base is almost completely cornered.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 13:52:47)

I’m trying to turn the right pincer from a “good local picture” into a real reduction lemma: either the late-\(v_5\) corner is truly dead, or there is one precise hidden hypothesis still missing.

_Thought for 48s_

I think the right pincer is now essentially **locally closed near the centered base**, modulo one formalization lemma.

The cleanest attack result is this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Near the centered diagonal base, the entire late-}v_5\text{ corner is locally harmless.}
}
\]

More precisely:

### 1. The \(u_5\)-patch is automatic

The centered witness gives
\[
U_1\neq 0,
\]
so
\[
u_5(s)=U_1s+U_3s^3+\cdots
\]
has a simple odd zero at the centered base. Since
\[
c(s)=C_0+O(s^2),\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
the quotient
\[
y:=\frac{u_5}{c}
\]
is an odd local coordinate. So the \(u_5\)-patch is already open locally, with no further theorem needed. turn123file9turn123file0

### 2. If \(v_5\) starts late, the \(u_5\)-patch germ has odd/odd shape

Assume the preferred \(v_5\)-route degenerates:
\[
\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3.
\]
On the \(u_5\)-patch define
\[
x(y):=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
\tau_u(y):=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}.
\]
Because \(v_5\) is odd and \(c\) is even, \(x(y)\) is odd, and
\[
x(y)=O(y^{2r+1}),
\]
so it is at least cubic. Because \(\Delta_7\) is even while \(c\) is even and \(u_5\) is odd, \(\tau_u\) is also odd. Subtract its linear part:
\[
\widetilde\tau_u(y):=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)\,y.
\]
Then \(\widetilde\tau_u\) is odd and either identically zero or of odd order at least \(3\). So after this affine normalization the local germ is
\[
\widetilde Q_u(y)=\bigl(y,\ x(y),\ \widetilde\tau_u(y)\bigr),
\]
with the last two channels odd and of order at least \(3\) whenever nonzero. turn123file14

### 3. After swapping coordinates, this is exactly the old odd/odd sterile model

Apply the ambient linear permutation
\[
(y,x,\widetilde\tau_u)\longmapsto (x,y,\widetilde\tau_u).
\]
Affine coplanarity / tangent-plane incidence are unchanged by such a map, so the local \(4\)-point obstruction problem is the same. After the swap, and after subtracting a suitable odd multiple if the two higher-order channels share the same leading odd order, the germ reduces to either
\[
(y^n,\ y,\ y^m),
\qquad
n>m\ge 3,\quad m,n\ \text{odd},
\]
or an even simpler degenerate case with one higher-order channel identically zero. But the centered diagonal-base exclusion theorem is already a sterility theorem for exactly this odd/odd normal form. So no mixed low-order obstruction points are born in that late-\(v_5\) corner. turn123file12

### 4. So the right pincer gives the sharp local reduction

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }\ord_s v_5\ge 3\text{ is odd, then that branch is locally sterile on the automatic }u_5\text{-patch.}
}
\]

Therefore the only mixed local branch still worth studying near the centered base is

\[
\boxed{
\ord_s v_5=1.
}
\]

And on that branch,
\[
v_5(s)=V_1s+V_3s^3+\cdots,\qquad V_1\neq 0,
\]
so
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5}{c}=X_1s+X_3s^3+\cdots,\qquad X_1=\frac{V_1}{C_0}\neq 0,
\]
hence the good \(v_5\)-patch is already open locally. That is exactly the branch the left pincer wants. turn123file10

## What is still not fully theorem-level

Only one thing:

\[
\boxed{
\text{formalize as a lemma that the odd/odd exclusion proof is invariant under this }Q_u\text{-patch affine normalization.}
}
\]

I do **not** think full patch-invariance of all \(Q_v\)-based formulas is needed. The weaker statement is enough:

> if a \(u_5\)-patch germ can be taken by ambient affine normalization into the same odd/odd local model already treated at the centered base, then the same punctured-neighborhood sterility conclusion applies.

That is the one remaining formal step on my side.

So my honest attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The right pincer has reduced the mixed local problem near the centered base to the single branch }\ord_s v_5=1.
}
\]

Everything with \(\ord_s v_5\ge 3\) should now be viewed as locally dead, pending only that affine-normalization transplant lemma.

That is now the right division of labor. 

I think the strongest new right-pincer sharpening is this:

on the \(u_5\)-patch, after setting
\[
y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
x(y)=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
\tau_u(y)=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5},
\]
the late-\(v_5\) corner is controlled entirely by the odd germ
\[
\widetilde\tau_u(y):=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)\,y.
\]

That gives a **two-subcase** reduction:

### Subcase A: \(\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0\)

Then after the fixed ambient coordinate swap
\[
(y,x,\widetilde\tau_u)\mapsto(x,y,\widetilde\tau_u),
\]
and subtraction of a suitable odd multiple if the two higher-order channels share the same leading odd order, the germ reduces to the same odd/odd local normal form already known to be punctured-neighborhood sterile. So this whole subcase should be dead. 

### Subcase B: \(\widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0\)

This is the sharper residual corner. It means
\[
\tau_u(y)=a\,y
\]
for some constant \(a\), equivalently
\[
-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}=a\,\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2.
\]

So the late-\(v_5\) corner is now reduced to one explicit algebraic relation:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_7\ \text{is locally proportional to }u_5^2\text{ on the }u_5\text{-patch.}
}
\]

That is much narrower than anything we had earlier. 

So my updated right-pincer map is:

- the clean branch \(V_1\neq 0\) belongs entirely to the left pincer;
- the late-\(v_5\) branch splits into:
  - \(\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0\), which should die by the odd/odd sterility transplant;
  - \(\widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0\), i.e.
    \[
    \Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2,
    \]
    which is the **only** residual mixed local corner I still see near the centered base. 

So the strongest final statement of the pincer is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Left pincer handles the clean }V_1\neq 0\text{ branch on the }v_5\text{-patch.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Right pincer handles the late-}V_1=0\text{ branch on the }u_5\text{-patch, except possibly the special relation }\Delta_7\propto u_5^2.
}
\]

That means the mixed local picture near the centered base is no longer diffuse. It has been reduced to one tiny residual corner:

\[
\boxed{
V_1=0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2
\ \text{locally on the }u_5\text{-patch.}
}
\]

That is the next exact theorem I would attack on the right side.

So my immediate next target is:

> **Residual-corner lemma.**  
> Rule out, or exploit to contradiction, the special local relation
> \[
> \Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2
> \]
> on the \(u_5\)-patch near the centered base.

If that lemma falls, then I think the mixed local branch near the centered base is essentially exhausted.
